    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2732856456" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2732856456" />
    <a title="Danielle Bodnar" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15311713-danielle-bodnar"><img alt="Danielle Bodnar" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1367796994p2/15311713.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2732856456?book_show_action=true">Apr 29, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Danielle Bodnar" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Danielle Bodnar" href="/user/show/15311713-danielle-bodnar">Danielle Bodnar</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2732856456" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13226014681866709191">Reading these novels has been a journey. I've been swept up in these characters' lives for almost two months, and the end leaves me with mixed feelings. I was at times exuberant with joy, righteously angry, frustrated with Lenu and Lila's choices at various points, and especially by Lila's coy reticence. I was also at times struck with anxiety and a soft sadness. In other words, these books have made me feel like no book has in some time. I've been so immersed in their stories I feel like a part</span>
  <span id="freeText13226014681866709191" style="display:none">Reading these novels has been a journey. I've been swept up in these characters' lives for almost two months, and the end leaves me with mixed feelings. I was at times exuberant with joy, righteously angry, frustrated with Lenu and Lila's choices at various points, and especially by Lila's coy reticence. I was also at times struck with anxiety and a soft sadness. In other words, these books have made me feel like no book has in some time. I've been so immersed in their stories I feel like a part of the neighborhood.<br /><br />What's interesting is that the details are spare, and most events are quickly summarized, but Ferrante still gets into the marrow of human emotions and relations. The subtleties beneath seemingly insignificant phrases or gestures are noted in detail and with keen insight. The sense of place is strong even if we don't have every brick of the stradone described in minute detail. Such description can be embedded with deeper meaning, but that is not Lenu's way. Her descriptions would merely scratch the surface. What she really gets into is more ephemeral, even though it permeates every aspect of a person's life. This insight gave me a strong sense of the characters, time, and place. I know Naples (and Italy) better than if I had ever visited it alone. The lack of detailed physical description also speaks true to life. It's been scientifically shown that the last vestiges of any memory are the emotions one felt. That is why emotionally charged moments endure - and even if one person didn't feel anything the other might have, creating a piecemeal patchwork of personal history. These are the moments that matter. <br /><br />As a woman and as a member of western society I highlighted so many passages. Though the book chronicles a friendship, it also covers six decades of Italy, as well as all the political and social turmoil that came with it. There's also a ton of feminist themes going on, and pretty much all the male characters act as chauvinists at some point, in a perfectly relatable way. Oftentimes the personal is indeed political, and the narrator herself acknowledges that she is a product of her class, place, and time. It only adds another intriguing layer to the already complex relationships chronicled in the books.<br /><br />If I have anything to critique, it's that it almost goes by too fast, and the final section of the final book is more sad than anything else. But that's life, I suppose. The ending is also unsatisfying in a way, and yet it also is satisfying. Some mysteries of life will never be solved. As Lenu writes, "the passage of time offers obscurity, not clarity." One thing is clear: the story chronicles a friendship, from its beginning to its end.<br /><br />One other thing I found bothersome may have to do with the translation, or the fact that I read all four so quickly in rapid succession. I saw a lot of "overdid it"s and "I was/became depressed" with no further elaboration. Of course to elaborate each time would have been wasteful, but phrases like that did seem repetitive. What does it mean to overdo it and to become depressed (not clinically)? There were also some turns of phrase that made me question mark. But again, this may be the fault of the translation and not the original story itself.<br /><br />This is the real-est realistic fiction that I have read in a long time. It made me wonder if some of these events had actually happened. But it doesn't matter. I would gladly dive into these novels again and sift more thoughtfully through the text. I find the saga worthy of five stars even if the story is imperfect. Then again, what isn't?</span>
  <a data-text-id="13226014681866709191" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2118366717" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2118366717" />
    <a title="Tess Evans" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/39138157-tess-evans"><img alt="Tess Evans" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442513985p2/39138157.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2118366717?book_show_action=true">Sep 08, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tess Evans" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tess Evans" href="/user/show/39138157-tess-evans">Tess Evans</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2118366717" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11374675249454708859">Housebound after spinal surgery, I came upon these novels. They are riveting in their evocation of Neapolitan life from the fifties to the present day. The detail is exquisite and the characters explored with a rare and touching intimacy. Each paragraph is crafted with care and many times I reread passages, not just for meaning but for the expression. Ferrante is fortunate to have a translator who seems so attuned to her writing. While this is an assumption on my part, I have to say that nowhere</span>
  <span id="freeText11374675249454708859" style="display:none">Housebound after spinal surgery, I came upon these novels. They are riveting in their evocation of Neapolitan life from the fifties to the present day. The detail is exquisite and the characters explored with a rare and touching intimacy. Each paragraph is crafted with care and many times I reread passages, not just for meaning but for the expression. Ferrante is fortunate to have a translator who seems so attuned to her writing. While this is an assumption on my part, I have to say that nowhere was I aware of a false note or something effortful or laboured. I had to slow down my reading of the last book because I didn't want to leave the deeply felt world of Lila and Lenu. It's quite a journey.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11374675249454708859" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3649102868" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3649102868" />
    <a title="Emma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/124773670-emma"><img alt="Emma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605643535p2/124773670.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3649102868?book_show_action=true">Nov 17, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emma" href="/user/show/124773670-emma">Emma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9789123473151" href="/book/show/33605716-neapolitan-novels-series-elena-ferrante-collection-4-books-bundle">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3649102868" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5430673082310348222">This tetralogy, written by the Italian writer Elena Ferrante (her identity is not very clear), is a beautiful travel around a indissoluble bond. The story takes place in Italy, exactly in Naples, in the 1950s and 1960s. It was very hard for me to understand the friendship between the two main characters: Lila and Lenù. They’ve shared their entire life: their childhood in the ‘rione’, their adolescence with their first experiences, their first approach to the university/ job and their maturity wi</span>
  <span id="freeText5430673082310348222" style="display:none">This tetralogy, written by the Italian writer Elena Ferrante (her identity is not very clear), is a beautiful travel around a indissoluble bond. The story takes place in Italy, exactly in Naples, in the 1950s and 1960s. It was very hard for me to understand the friendship between the two main characters: Lila and Lenù. They’ve shared their entire life: their childhood in the ‘rione’, their adolescence with their first experiences, their first approach to the university/ job and their maturity with their families. I recommend these four books especially to Italian people but also to foreign people which want to read a very beautiful story of friendship, family and social redemption!!!</span>
  <a data-text-id="5430673082310348222" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2820613310" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2820613310" />
    <a title="Mona Nomura" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26104302-mona-nomura"><img alt="Mona Nomura" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1498365535p2/26104302.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2820613310?book_show_action=true">May 14, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mona Nomura" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mona Nomura" href="/user/show/26104302-mona-nomura">Mona Nomura</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2820613310" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18401258975776561043">I’ve never read a book, more or less a series, where I had zero attachments to any of the characters but could not put it down. <br/><br/>Like a classic piece of music, starts slow and crescendos, hence this five year tardy to the party completion. <br/><br/>Dark, powerful, brutally honest, a once in a lifetime story from a once in a generation storyteller. <br/><br/>100% recommended. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Moony" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Moony" href="/user/show/59265845-moony">Moony</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9788866328087" href="/book/show/40027936-l-amica-geniale-edizione-completa">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/59265845-moony?shelf=lang-italiano">lang-italiano</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/59265845-moony?shelf=coming-of-age">coming-of-age</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3596589708" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15239484709945178617">I have a feeling the average rating of this series would be much different if I'd read the volumes separately. The ending (to be exact, the second half of the fourth book) was frankly underwhelming, but it's a story that spans a lifetime, and it's hard for me when reading something of this scope and length not to feel a bit in awe. <br/><br/>(really, though, what was up with the part about Elena's daughters?)</span>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('tlDtLuD0gX1vDoCEbvsr6olhR2VxAIhQNOFOAm8PVcpXgD4r/gxiEPeDVlSR0mzAeMpFrqa8he48eiKOHMqW6g==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ISqdfaVywGf1ob0mzxVCinr1vsJFaWR19DCqUUILlB/A+k54u4ojCm0sa/YwPAWgi168CZLVacv8q8bdMc5XPw==')})
  }
//]]>

Still, when detectives asked for victims to come forward, she sent a note.\n\nHer criminal case file reopened, she saw for the first time evidence that corroborated her memories. Here were depictions of the naïve, hard-working girl she\'d been, a chorister and debater, the daughter of a priest; of the two senior athletes who assaulted her and were allowed to graduate with awards; and of the faculty, doctors, and priests who had known about Crawford\'s assault and gone to great lengths to bury it.\n\nNow a wife, mother, and writer living on the other side of the country, Crawford learned that police had uncovered astonishing proof of an institutional silencing years before, and that unnamed powers were still trying to block her case. The slander, innuendo, and lack of adult concern that Crawford had experienced as a student hadn\'t been imagined as the effects of trauma, after all: these were the actions of a school that prized its reputation above anything, even a child.\n\nThis revelation launched Crawford on an extraordinary inquiry into the ways gender, privilege, and power shaped her experience as a girl at the gates of America\'s elite. Her investigation looks beyond the sprawling playing fields and soaring chapel towers of crucibles of power like St. Paul\'s, whose reckoning is still to come. And it runs deep into the channels of shame and guilt, witness and silencing, that dictate who can speak and who is heard in American society.\n\nAn insightful, mature, beautifully written memoir, Notes on a Silencing is an arresting coming-of-age story that wrestles with an essential question for our time: what telling of a survivor\'s story will finally force a remedy?<\/span>\n  <a Well-nigh unfathomable problems lead to measures that seem like emergency operations on the open heart of the Western world, performed with no knowledge of the patient\'s clinical history. The gravity of the situation is matched by the paucity of our understanding of it, and of how it came about in the first place.In this book, compiled from his Adorno Lectures given in Frankfurt, Wolfgang Streeck lays bare the roots of the present financial, fiscal and economic crisis, seeing it as part of the long neoliberal transformation of postwar capitalism that began in the 1970s. Linking up with the crisis theories of that decade, he analyses the subsequent tensions and conflicts involving states, governments, voters and capitalist interests—a process in which the defining focus of the European state system has shifted from taxation through debt to budgetary “consolidation.” The book then ends by exploring the prospects for a restoration of social and economic stability. Buying Time is a model of enlightenment. The disconnect between our experience of the world and the economic model used to explain it has given rise to &quot;angrynomics&quot;: an economy of heightened uncertainty and anger, where faith in the workings of markets and politics has been undermined and rapid and seemingly ever-accelerating economic change has become something to be feared.\n\nEric Lonergan and Mark Blyth have written a book for anyone anxious, worried – or angry – about the mismatch between how they experience the world with the increasing day to day pressures they face and the model used by economic elites and politicians to explain and justify it. La ciudad vive días de gran agitación social. La oscura miseria de los más desfavorecidos contrasta con la elegante opulencia de las grandes avenidas, donde ya destacan algunos edificios singulares, símbolo de la llegada del Modernismo. Dalmau Sala, hijo de un anarquista ajusticiado, es un joven pintor que vive atrapado entre dos mundos. Por un lado, su familia y Emma, la mujer que ama, son firmes defensores de la lucha obrera; hombres y mujeres que no conocen el miedo a la hora de exigir los derechos de los trabajadores. Por otro, su trabajo en el taller de cerámica de don Manuel Bello, su mentor y un conservador burgués de férreas creencias católicas, lo acerca a un ambiente donde imperan la riqueza y la innovación creativa. De este modo, seducido por las tentadoras ofertas de una burguesía dispuesta a comprar su obra y su conciencia, Dalmau tendrá que encontrar su auténtico camino, como hombre y como artista, y alejarse de las noches de vino y drogas para descubrir lo que de verdad le importa: sus valores, su esencia, el amor de una mujer valiente y luchadora y, sobre todo, esos cuadros que brotan de su imaginación y capturan en un lienzo las almas más miserables que deambulan por las calles de una ciudad agitada por el germen de la rebeldía. \n  Con\n  \n     El pintor de almas\n  \n  , Ildefonso Falcones nos ofrece la poderosa historia de una época convulsa al tiempo que nos brinda una trama emocionante donde el amor, la pasión por el arte, la lucha por los ideales y la venganza se combinan con maestría para recrear una Barcelona, antaño sobria y gris, que ahora se encamina haciaun futuro brillante donde el color y la esperanza empiezan a extenderse por sus casas y sus calles.\n La crítica ha dicho:«Rápida y vertiginosa en su trama, describe a su vez sensacionalmente bien cómo se fue construyendo nuestra ciudad, la lucha de clases o la lucha entre estilos arquitectónicos. Engancha desde la primera página. Ildefonso Falcones es el mejor escritor de novela histórica de España en este siglo, así de sencillo y así de categórico.»José Mª Fuster-Fabra, La Razón Cataluña «Personajes muy bien trabajados e información precisa, clara y algo arcádica de un momento que al lector le fascina: placer y aprendizaje al mismo tiempo [...] El pintor de almas se despliega con todo su poder de fascinación. ¿Quién se resiste a darle un bocado?»Juan Ángel Juristo, Abc Cultural Lo que ha dicho la crítica sobre La catedral del mar:«De Barcelona ya conocíamos la Sagrada Familia, la delirante catedral del arquitecto Gaudí. <span id="freeTextContainer5833468055178355093">Elena Ferrante is a pseudonymous Italian novelist. Ferrante's books, originally published in Italian, have been translated into many languages. Her four-book series of Neapolitan Novels are her most widely known works.</span>

<script>
//<![CDATA[
      var newTip = new Tip($('bookCover_17465515'), "\n\n  <h2><a class=\"readable bookTitle\" href=\"https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17465515-the-story-of-a-new-name?from_choice=false&amp;from_home_module=false\">The Story of a New Name<\/a><\/h2>\n\n      <div>\n        by <a class=\"authorName\" href=\"/author/show/44085.Elena_Ferrante?origin=series_works\">Elena Ferrante<\/a>\n      <\/div>\n\n          <div class=\"smallText uitext darkGreyText\">\n            <span class=\"minirating\"><span class=\"stars staticStars notranslate\"><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p3\"><\/span><\/span> 4.39 avg rating &mdash; 109,875 ratings<\/span>            &mdash; published 2012\n          <\/div>\n\n    <div class=\"addBookTipDescription\">\n      \n<span id=\"freeTextContainer11993490051291140310\">In 2012, Elena Ferrante\'s My Brilliant Friend introduced readers to the unforgettable Elena and Lila, whose lifelong friendship provides the backbone for the Neapolitan Novels. The Story of a New Name is the second book in this series. With these boo<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText11993490051291140310\" style=\"display:none\">In 2012, Elena Ferrante\'s My Brilliant Friend introduced readers to the unforgettable Elena and Lila, whose lifelong friendship provides the backbone for the Neapolitan Novels. The Story of a New Name is the second book in this series. With these books, which the New Yorker\'s James Wood described as &quot;large, captivating, amiably peopled ... a beautiful and delicate tale of confluence and reversal,&quot; Ferrante proves herself to be one of Italy\'s most accomplished storytellers. She writes vividly about a specific neighborhood of Naples from the late-1950s through to the current day and about two remarkable young women who are very much the products of that place and time. Yet in doing so she has created a world in which readers will recognize themselves and has drawn a marvelously nuanced portrait of friendship.\n\nIn The Story of a New Name, Lila has recently married and made her entrée into the family business; Elena, meanwhile, continues her studies and her exploration of the world beyond the neighborhood that she so often finds stifling. Love, jealousy, family, freedom, commitment, and above all friendship: these are signs under which both women live out this phase in their stories. Marriage appears to have imprisoned Lila, and the pressure to excel is at times too much for Elena. Yet the two young women share a complex and evolving bond that is central to their emotional lives and is a source of strength in the face of life\'s challenges.
